## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models reaction rate dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as polynomial or power-law functions of concentration, with possible time-dependent terms for non-autonomous systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order / Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Second-order with linear term: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (trimolecular reaction)
- Quadratic with constant: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (polynomial rate law with source/sink)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated first-order kinetics)
- Michaelis-Menten variant: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order saturation kinetics)
- Competing pathways with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Power-law with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate law with background)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power dependence on concentration → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power (mass action kinetics)
- Negative rate constant sign → consumption/decay of reactant rather than production
- Rational function of concentration (A/(c+A)) → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with site saturation
- Product of concentration and (constant - concentration) terms → autocatalytic or logistic growth kinetics with finite carrying capacity
- Polynomial in A with multiple terms → parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms of different orders
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system consistent with standard mass-action kinetics
- Explicit time dependence (e.g., exp(c*t) multiplier) → externally driven system, photolysis, or time-varying temperature/catalyst
- Fractional power of concentration (A**0.5) → chain reaction mechanisms or diffusion-limited surface reactions
- Sum of negative power-law terms → complex mechanism where multiple elementary steps contribute with different concentration dependencies
- Concentration squared minus linear term (c0*A**2 + c1*A) → reversible bimolecular reaction or dimerization equilibrium
